# LoCoBench-Agent Task

## Task Information

**Task ID**: rust_api_microservice_expert_008_architectural_understanding_expert_01
**Category**: architectural_understanding
**Difficulty**: expert
**Language**: rust
**Context Length**: 1014465 tokens
**Files**: 85

## Task Title

Architectural Analysis and Redesign for Cache Invalidation in a Rust Microservice

## Description

LedgerLink Nexus is a high-performance Rust-based financial data API microservice. To handle high read loads, the system implements a sophisticated response caching layer. A critical bug report has emerged: clients are intermittently receiving stale data for resources that have been recently updated. This issue persists until the cache entry's Time-To-Live (TTL) expires. As a senior architect, your task is to analyze the system's architecture, pinpoint the root cause of this data consistency problem, and propose a robust architectural solution.

## Your Task

You are tasked with resolving a critical stale data issue in the LedgerLink Nexus service. Your analysis and proposal should be based entirely on the provided source files.

1.  **Analyze the System**: Examine the provided source code to understand the overall architecture. Given the obfuscated filenames, you must infer the purpose of each module from its content.
2.  **Identify Key Components**: Pinpoint the specific modules responsible for the following functions:
    *   a) The core response caching logic.
    *   b) Handling incoming read requests (e.g., `GET` operations).
    *   c) Handling incoming write requests (e.g., `POST`, `PUT`, `DELETE` operations).
3.  **Diagnose the Flaw**: Clearly describe the fundamental architectural flaw that causes the stale data issue. Explain *why* updating a resource does not immediately reflect in subsequent read requests.
4.  **Propose a Solution**: Design an architectural solution to ensure cache consistency. Do not write the full implementation. Instead, describe the design pattern you would employ (e.g., explicit invalidation, write-through caching). Justify your choice.
5.  **Outline Implementation Plan**: List the specific modules that would require modification to implement your proposed solution. Describe the new interactions that must be established between these modules (e.g., which module calls which, and with what information).

## Expected Approach

An expert developer would approach this task systematically:

1.  **Initial Reconnaissance**: The developer would start by inspecting `package.json` to identify the web framework (e.g., `actix-web`, `axum`) and caching libraries (e.g., `redis`, `moka`). They would then review `src/config.txt` to find configuration parameters related to caching (like TTLs, Redis connection strings) and other services.
2.  **Trace Request Lifecycle**: The next step is to find the application's entry point (e.g., a `main` function initializing the server). This would reveal the middleware pipeline, providing clues about the modules responsible for logging, authentication, and caching.
3.  **Module Identification via Keywords & Patterns**:
    *   **Caching Module**: The developer would search across all `src/*.txt` files for keywords like `cache`, `redis`, `get`, `set`, `ttl`, and patterns related to the identified caching library. This would lead them to the module(s) encapsulating caching logic.
    *   **Handler Modules**: They would search for web framework macros or function signatures that define routes (e.g., `#[get("/...")]`, `#[post("/...")]`, `web::resource(...).to(...)`). This would identify the modules handling HTTP requests.
    *   **Distinguish Read/Write**: Within the handler modules, the developer would differentiate between read (`GET`) and write (`POST`, `PUT`, `DELETE`) operations based on the HTTP method specified in the route definition.
4.  **Connect the Dots & Identify the Flaw**: The developer would trace the logic for a typical `GET` request, noting its interaction with the caching module (a `cache.get()` call). Then, they would trace a `PUT` or `POST` request for a similar resource, observing that while it interacts with a database or data source, it makes *no corresponding call* to the caching module to update or invalidate the now-stale entry. This absence of interaction is the core architectural flaw.
5.  **Formulate the Architectural Fix**: The developer would propose a direct cache invalidation strategy. They would suggest modifying the write handlers to explicitly call an `invalidate(key)` or `delete(key)` function on the caching service after a successful database write. They would justify this as a robust, immediate, and targeted solution, superior to simply lowering the cache TTL.
6.  **Plan the Changes**: Finally, they would specify that the identified write-handler module(s) need to be changed to call a new function in the identified caching module. The plan would detail that the write handler needs to construct the correct cache key (the same key the `GET` handler uses) and pass it to the new invalidation function.

## Evaluation Criteria

- **Component Identification Accuracy**: Did the agent correctly identify the primary modules for caching, read handling, and write handling (`module_44`, `module_26`/`52`, `module_71`)?
- **Flaw Diagnosis Clarity**: Was the agent able to articulate that the problem is the *absence of an invalidation signal* from the write handlers to the cache, rather than a bug in the caching logic itself?
- **Solution Robustness**: Did the agent propose a robust architectural pattern like explicit invalidation? Points are deducted for simplistic or ineffective solutions like 'just lower the cache TTL'.
- **Implementation Plan Correctness**: Did the agent correctly identify that both the write handler module and the caching service module require modification?
- **Interaction Description**: Did the agent clearly describe the new required interaction: the write handler calling an invalidation function in the cache service after a successful DB write?
- **Reasoning Quality**: Does the agent's justification for its proposed solution demonstrate an understanding of trade-offs in distributed systems (e.g., consistency vs. performance)?

     1→```rust
     2→//! src/module_52.txt
     3→//!
     4→//! High-frequency, paginated read-model for ledger entries with
     5→//!  * request validation
     6→//!  * Redis response-caching
     7→//!  * repository abstraction (Postgres backing store)
     8→//!  * structured error envelopes
     9→//!  * tracing instrumentation
    10→//!
    11→//! This module purposefully lives in its own compilation unit so it can be
    12→//! reused by both the REST and GraphQL façades without creating a hard
    13→//! dependency on either transport layer.
    14→

73-assistanttext-
I have completed the architectural analysis of the LedgerLink Nexus cache invalidation issue. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Analysis Complete

### Key Findings

1. **Core Problem Identified**: The stale data issue is caused by **missing cache invalidation in write handlers**. Read operations (`GET`) cache responses in Redis, but write operations (`POST`, `PUT`, `DELETE`) do not invalidate or update the corresponding cache entries.

2. **Key Components Identified**:
   - **Caching modules**: `module_44` (primary caching for ledger entries), `module_46` (pagination-aware cache with eviction support), `module_33` (ResponseCache trait)
   - **Read handlers**: `module_26`, `module_52`, `module_71` (all implement cache-aside pattern)
   - **Write handlers**: `module_38` (writes to DB without invalidating cache), `module_67` (exception - properly invalidates cache)

3. **Architectural Flaw**: The system follows CQRS principles and has cache invalidation infrastructure (`PagedCache::evict()`, `ResponseCache::invalidate()`), but write handlers are not wired to use these methods. This creates a classic cache coherence problem.

4. **Proposed Solution**: Explicit Cache Invalidation pattern - modify all write handlers to call cache invalidation after successful database writes, using key pattern matching (e.g., `tenant:{id}:*`) for efficient bulk eviction.

5. **Implementation Plan**: 
   - Modify `module_38` (and similar write handlers) to inject cache dependency and call invalidation
   - Add `invalidate_tenant_entries()` method to `module_44`
   - Leverage existing pub/sub infrastructure in `module_46` for distributed cache coherence

The complete solution has been written to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with detailed code evidence, analysis, and implementation recommendatio

  "file_path": "/app/project/src/config.txt"

{
  "file": {
    "content": "```rust\n//! src/config.rs\n//!\n//! Centralized configuration loader for the **LedgerLink Nexus** API micro-service.\n//!\n//! The configuration system fulfils a few non-functional requirements:\n//!  1. Environment-aware (local, staging, production, \u2026) overrides  \n//!  2. Secrets stay out of Git\u2014use `$APP_\u2026` env vars instead  \n//!  3. Strongly-typed settings with fall-back defaults + robust error handling  \n//!  4. Hot-reload friendly (watch the file + refresh cache) *(behind feature flag)*  \n//!\n//! The module exposes an [`AppConfig`] root object that can be queried from anywhere\n//! in the application. Internally it lazily loads a singleton via [`once_cell`],\n//! thus preventing configuration scattering / needless file-IO on hot paths.\n//!\n//! Example:\n//! ```no_run\n//! let cfg = ledgerlink_nexus::config::get();\n//! tracing::info!(bind = ?cfg.http.bind, \"\ud83d\ude80  HTTP server starting\");\n//! ```\n\nuse std::{net::IpAddr, path::Path, sync::Arc, time::Duration};\n\nuse config::{Config, ConfigError, Environment, File};\nuse once_cell::sync::OnceCell;\nuse secrecy::{ExposeSecret, SecretString};\nuse serde::Deserialize;\nuse thiserror::Error;\n\n/// Retrieve the global, lazily-initialised [`AppConfig`].\n///\n/// # Panics\n/// The function panics if configuration loading fails **once** at startup.\n/// Subsequent calls are guaranteed not to panic.\npub fn get() -> &'static AppConfig {\n    static INSTANCE: OnceCell<AppConfig> = OnceCell::new();\n    INSTANCE.get_or_init(|| match AppConfig::load() {\n        Ok(cfg) => cfg,\n        Err(e) => {\n            // A config load failure is considered unrecoverable.\n            eprintln!(\"\u274c Failed to load configuration: {:?}\", e);\n            std::process::exit(1);\n        }\n    })\n}\n\n/// Shallow clone wrapper around [`get`].\n/// Useful when configuration needs to be shared across async tasks.\npub fn shared() -> Arc<AppConfig> {\n    Arc::new(get().clone())\n}\n\n/// Complete application configuration (root).\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\n#[serde(rename_all = \"snake_case\")]\npub struct AppConfig {\n    pub http: HttpConfig,\n    pub postgres: PostgresConfig,\n    pub redis: RedisConfig,\n    pub auth: AuthConfig,\n    pub pagination: PaginationConfig,\n    pub caching: ResponseCacheConfig,\n    pub logging: LoggingConfig,\n}\n\nimpl AppConfig {\n    /// Load configuration from the following sources **in order**:\n    ///  1. `config/default.{toml,yaml,json}` (optional)\n    ///  2. `config/{RUN_MODE}.{toml,yaml,json}` where `RUN_MODE=$APP_ENV` (optional)\n    ///  3. Environment variables (`APP__POSTGRES__HOST=\u2026`)\n    ///\n    /// The merge strategy is \u201clast one wins\u201d.\n    pub fn load() -> Result<Self, ConfigLoadError> {\n        let env = std::env::var(\"APP_ENV\").unwrap_or_else(|_| \"local\".into());\n        let mut cfg = Config::builder();\n\n        // tier 1\n        cfg = cfg.add_source(File::with_name(\"config/default\").required(false));\n\n        // tier 2\n        cfg = cfg.add_source(File::with_name(&format!(\"config/{}\", env)).required(false));\n\n        // tier 3 (env vars). Double underscore `__` = nesting delimiter.\n        cfg = cfg.add_source(\n            Environment::with_prefix(\"APP\")\n                .separator(\"__\")\n                .list_separator(\",\"),\n        );\n\n        // finish\n        cfg.build()\n            .map_err(ConfigLoadError::Parse)?\n            .try_deserialize::<AppConfig>()\n            .map_err(ConfigLoadError::Deserialize)\n    }\n}\n\n/// Errors that might occur while loading the configuration.\n#[derive(Debug, Error)]\npub enum ConfigLoadError {\n    #[error(\"config file parsing failed: {0}\")]\n    Parse(ConfigError),\n    #[error(\"config deserialization failed: {0}\")]\n    Deserialize(ConfigError),\n}\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/*                               Sub-structures                               */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\npub struct HttpConfig {\n    #[serde(default = \"default_bind_addr\")]\n    pub bind: IpAddr,\n    #[serde(default = \"default_port\")]\n    pub port: u16,\n    #[serde(default = \"default_request_timeout_secs\")]\n    pub request_timeout: Duration,\n    #[serde(default)]\n    pub enable_graphql_playground: bool,\n}\n\nfn default_bind_addr() -> IpAddr {\n    IpAddr::from([0, 0, 0, 0])\n}\nfn default_port() -> u16 {\n    8080\n}\nfn default_request_timeout_secs() -> Duration {\n    Duration::from_secs(30)\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\npub struct PostgresConfig {\n    pub host: String,\n    #[serde(default = \"default_pg_port\")]\n    pub port: u16,\n    pub dbname: String,\n    pub username: String,\n    #[serde(deserialize_with = \"deser_secret\")]\n    pub password: SecretString,\n    #[serde(default = \"default_pg_pool_size\")]\n    pub max_pool_size: u32,\n    #[serde(default)]\n    pub require_ssl: bool,\n}\n\nfn default_pg_port() -> u16 {\n    5432\n}\nfn default_pg_pool_size()   if *per_page == 0 || *per_page > MAX_PER_PAGE {\n            return Err(ValidationError::new(\"per_page_out_of_range\"));\n        }\n    }\n    Ok(())\n}\n\nimpl Default for ListQuery {\n    fn FromRequestParts<S> for JwtAuth\nwhere\n    S: Send + Sync,\n{\n    type Rejection = ApiError;\n\n    async fn from_request_parts(parts: &mut Parts, _state: &S) -> Result<Self, Self::Rejection> {\n        let TypedHeader(Authorization(bearer)) =\n            TypedHeader::<Authorization<Bearer>>::from_request_parts(parts, _state)\n                .await\n                .map_err(|_| \"tenant:<tenant_id>:user:<user_id>\"\n        let mut iter = token_str.split(':');\n        let prefix = iter.next().unwrap_or_default();\n        if prefix != \"tenant\" {\n            return Err(ApiError::unauthorized());\n        }\n        let tenant_id = iter\n            .next()\n            .and_then(|s| Uuid::parse_str(s).ok())\n            .ok_or_else(ApiError::unauthorized)?;\n\n RepositoryError> {\n        let page = query.page.unwrap_or(1);\n        let per_page = query.per_page.unwrap_or(50) as i64;\n        let offset = ((page - 1) as i64) * per_page;\n\n        // Filtering\n        let (entries, total): (Vec<LedgerEntry>, i64) = if let Some(ref account) = query.account_code\n        {\n            let rows = sqlx::query_as::<_, LedgerEntry>(\n                r#\"\n                SELECT *\n                FROM ledger_entries\n                WHERE tenant_id = $1\n                  AND account_code = $2\n                ORDER BY occurred_at DESC\n                OFFSET $3\n                LIMIT $4\n                \"#,\n            )\n            .bind(tenant_id)\n            .bind(account)\n            .bind(offset)\n            .bind(per_page)\n            .fetch_all(&self.pool)\n            .await?;\n\n            let total: (i64,) = sqlx::query_as(\n                r#\"\n                SELECT COUNT(*) as count\n                FROM  .fetch_one(&self.pool)\n            .await?;\n\n            (rows, total.0)\n        } else {\n            let rows = sqlx::query_as::<_, LedgerEntry>(\n                r#\"\n                SELECT        )\n            .bind(tenant_id)\n            .bind(offset)\n            .bind(per_page)\n            .fetch_all(&self.pool)\n            .await?;\n\n            let total: (i64,) = sqlx::query_as(\n                r#\"\n                SELECT COUNT(*) as count\n                FROM ledger_entries\n                WHERE tenant_id = $1\n                \"#,\n            )\n            .bind(tenant_id)\n            .fetch_one(&self.pool)\n            .await?;\n\n            (rows, total.0)\n        };\n\n        Ok((entries, total as u64))\n #[instrument(skip(self))]\n    pub async fn list(\n        &self,\n        tenant: Uuid,\n        query: ListQuery,\n    ) -> Result<Paginated<LedgerEntryDto>, ServiceError> {\n        // 1. Try cache (30ms timeout to avoid head-of-line blocking)\n        let key = Self::cache_key(tenant, &query);\n        if let Ok(Some(raw)) = self.try_fetch_cache(&key).await {\n            debug!(%tenant, %key, \"Cache hit\");\n            return serde_json::from_slice::<Paginated<LedgerEntryDto>>(&raw)\n                .map_err(ServiceError::CacheSerialization);\n        }\n\n        // 2. ServiceError> {\n        let mut conn: RedisConn = self.redis.get().await?;\n        // short timeout to protect against redis hiccups\n        let result: Option<Vec<u8>> =\n            timeout(Duration::from_millis(30), conn.get(key)).await??;\n        Ok(result)\n    }\n\n    async fn persist_cache<T: Serialize>(&self, key: &str, value: &T) -> Result<(), ServiceError> {\n        let mut conn: RedisConn = self.redis.get().await?;\n        let data = serde_json::to_vec(value)?;\n        let _: () = conn\n            .set_ex(key, data, 60) // 60 seconds TTL\n            .await\n            .map_err(ServiceError::Cache)?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Error)]\npub enum ServiceError {\n    #[error(\"repository error: {0}\")]\n    Repo(#[from] This module is completely self-contained yet showcases the LedgerLink\n//! Nexus architecture principles:\n//!   \u2022 Clean separation between View (DTO)  \u279c  View-Model (validated\n//!     transport structs)  \u279c  Domain Models / Repository  \u279c  Service.\n//!   \u2022 Transparent response-caching with Redis using a typed cache key.\n//!   \u2022 Structured error handling with `thiserror` and `tracing`.\n//!   \u2022 Feature-gated compile options (`response_caching`) for optional\n//!     dependencies, keeping binary size and attack-surface minimal.\n//!\n//! Down-stream HTTP/GraphQL handlers can simply call\n//! `CashFlowForecastService::get_forecast(..)` and receive a fully\n//! validated, paginated & (optionally) cached payload ready to be\n//! Err(ValidationError::InvalidDateRange)\n        } else {\n            Ok(self)\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Simple pagination descriptor (page & per_page are both 1-based).\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, NonZeroU32::new(per_page).ok_or(ValidationError::InvalidPageSize)?;\n        Ok(Self { page, per_page })\n    }\n\n    #[inline]\n    pub fn offset(&self) -> u32 {\n        (self.page.get() - 1) * self.per_page.get()\n    }\n\n    #[inline]\n    pub fn limit(&self) -> u32 {\n        self.per_page.get()\n    }\n}\n\n/// Domain aggregate representing a single cash-flow forecast from(f: CashFlowForecast) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            id: f.id,\n            date: f.date,\n            expected_inflow: f.expected_inflow,\n            expected_outflow: f.expected_outflow,\n            currency: f.currency,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Output envelope with pagination metadata.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize)]\npub struct CashFlowForecastPage {\n    pub items: Vec<CashFlowForecastDto>,\n    pub total_items: u64,\n    pub page: u32,\n    pub per_page: u32,\n}\n\n/// Domain-driven repository abstraction.\n///\n/// Implementations live in separate crates (e.g. `ledgerlink_pg`) and can\n/// be swapped at runtime using dependency-injection.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait CashFlowForecastRepository: Send + Sync + 'static {\n    async fn fa\u00e7ade orchestrating query workflow.\npub struct CashFlowForecastService<R, C> {\n    repo: Arc<R>,\n    #[cfg(feature = \"response_caching\")]\n    cache: Arc<C>,\n    /// TTL for cache entries.\n    #[cfg(feature = \"response_caching\")]\n    ttl: Duration,\n}\n\nimpl<R, C> CashFlowForecastService<R, C>\nwhere\n    R: CashFlowForecastRepository,\n{\n    pub fn new(repo: Arc<R>) -> Self\n    where\n        C: Default,\n    {\n        Self {\n            repo,\n            #[cfg(feature = \"response_caching\")]\n            cache: Arc::<C>::default(),\n            #[cfg(feature = \"response_caching\")]\n            ttl: Duration::from_secs(300),\n        }\n    }\n\n    #[cfg_attr(\n        feature = \"response_caching\",\n        instrument(\n            name = \"CashFlowForecastService::get_forecast\",\n            skip(self),\n            fields(account_id = %account_id, page = pagination.page, per_page = pagination.per_page)\n        )\n    )]\n    #[cfg_attr(\n        not(feature = \"response_caching\"),\n        instrument(\n            name = \"CashFlowForecastService::get_forecast\",\n            skip(self),\n            fields(account_id = #[cfg(feature = \"response_caching\")]\n        if !force_refresh {\n            if let Some(cached) = self\n                .cache\n                .get::<CashFlowForecastPage>(&CacheKey::new(\n                    account_id,\n                    range,\n                    pagination,\n                ))\n                .await?\n            {\n                debug!(\"cache hit for started_at = Instant::now();\n        let (rows, total) = self\n            .repo\n            .list_by_account(account_id, range, pagination)\n            .await\n            .map_err(ServiceError::Repository)?;\n        debug!(\"db_query completed in {:?}\", started_at.elapsed());\n\n        let page = CashFlowForecastPage {\n            items: rows.into_iter().map(Into::into).collect(),\n            total_items: total,\n            page: pagination.page.get(),\n            per_page: pagination.per_page.get(),\n        };\n\n        #[cfg(feature = \"response_caching\")]\n        {\n            self.cache\n                .set(\n                    CacheKey::new(account_id, range, pagination),\n                    &page,\n                    self.ttl,\n                )\n                .await?;\n        }\n\n        Ok(page)\n    }\n}\n\n//\n// ----------------------------- Caching ----------------------------------\n//\n#[cfg(feature = \"response_caching\")]\n#[async_trait]\npub trait CacheBackend: Send + Sync + 'static {\n    async fn get<T>(&self, key: &CacheKey) -> -> Result<(), CacheError>\n    where\n        T: Serialize + Send + Sync;\n}\n\n/// Typed cache-key guaranteeing stable hash/serialize logic.\n#[cfg(feature = \"response_caching\")]\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Hash, PartialEq, Eq, Serialize)]\npub struct CacheKey {\n    account_id: Uuid,\n    from: NaiveDate,\n    to: NaiveDate,\n    page: u32,\n    per_page: u32,\n}\n\n#[cfg(feature = \"response_caching\")]\nimpl CacheKey {\n    pub fn new(\n        account_id: Uuid,\n        range: DateRange,\n        pagination: Pagination,\n    ) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            account_id,\n            from: range.from,\n            to: range.to,\n            page: pagination.page.get(),\n            per_page: pagination.per_page.get(),\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn self.to, self.page, self.per_page\n        )\n    }\n}\n\n/// Minimal Redis cache backend implementation.\n#[cfg(all(feature = \"response_caching\", feature = \"redis\"))]\npub struct RedisCache<B: ConnectionLike + Send + Sync + 'static>(pub tokio::sync::Mutex<B>);\n\n#[cfg(all(feature = \"response_caching\", feature = \"redis\"))]\n#[async_trait]\nimpl<B> CacheBackend for RedisCache<B>\nwhere\n    B: ConnectionLike + Send + Sync + 'static,\n{\n    async fn get<T>(&self, key: &CacheKey) -> Result<Option<T>, CacheError>\n    where\n        T: for<'de> Deserialize<'de> + Send,\n    {\n        let redis_key = key.as_redis_key();\n        let mut conn = self.0.lock().await;\n        let data: Option<String> = conn.get(&redis_key).await?;\n        Ok(match data {\n            Some(s) => {\n                let parsed = serde_json::from_str::<T>(&s)?;\n                Some(parsed)\n            }\n            None => None,\n        })\n    }\n\n    async fn set<T>(\n        &self,\n        key: CacheKey,\n        value: &T,\n        ttl: Duration,\n    ) -> Result<(), CacheError>\n    where\n        T: Serialize + Send + Sync,\n    {\n        let redis_key = key.as_redis_key();\n Getting Started\n2. Versioning Strategy\n3. Authentication & Authorization\n4. Error Handling Contract\n5. REST Endpoints\n   - Ledger Entries\n   - Account Snapshots\n   - Cash-Flow Forecasts\n6. GraphQL Endpoint\n7. Pagination & Caching\n8. Rate Limiting\n9. Observability & Tracing\n10. Changelog (v1.x)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Getting Started\nBase URL (production):\n\n```\nhttps://api.ledgerlink.io\n```\n\nSandbox (free tier):\n\n```\nhttps://sandbox.ledgerlink.io\n```\n\nAll requests **must** be served over HTTPS. HTTP requests return `426 Upgrade Required`.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Versioning Strategy\nLedgerLink Nexus follows a _media-type driven_ versioning model.\n\n```\nAccept: application/vnd.ledgerlink.v1+json\n```\n\nMajor version bumps are announced 90 days in advance via status page and in the `X-Deprecation` header.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Authentication & Authorization\nNexus supports two authentication flows:\n\n1. OAuth 2.1 Client Credentials (recommended)  \n2. Long-lived Service Tokens (legacy)\n\nInclude the token in the `Authorization` header:\n\n```\nAuthorization: Bearer <access_token>\n```\n\nScopes map one-to-one with CQRS command/query capabilities:\n\n| Scope                   | Grants                                       |\n|-------------------------|----------------------------------------------|\n| `ledgers:read`          | List / fetch ledger entries                  |\n| `ledgers:write`         | Create / update ledger entries               |\n| `accounts:read`         | Account snapshots & cash-flow forecasts      |\n| `webhooks:manage`       | Register, pause, delete webhooks             |\n\nA token with insufficient scopes returns:\n\n```\nHTTP/1.1 403 Forbidden\nLedger-Error-Code: AUTH_SCOPE_INSUFFICIENT\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Error Handling Contract\nLedgerLink uses structured JSON error envelopes inspired by RFC 7807.\n\n```json\n{\n  \"error\": {\n    \"code\": \"VALIDATION_FAILED\",\n    \"message\": \"Amount must be greater than zero\",\n    \"details\": [\n      {\n        \"field\": \"amount\",\n        \"issue\": \"must_be_positive\"\n      }\n    ],\n    \"correlation_id\": \"2d501f96-e65b-4b93-a7c8-a7269f30a8ea\",\n    \"timestamp\": \"2024-05-05T08:17:21.155Z\"\n  }\n}\n```\n\n| HTTP Status | Code Prefix        | Layer                       |\n|-------------|-------------------|-----------------------------|\n| 4xx         | VALIDATION / AUTH | Request validation, auth    |\n| 5xx         | INTERNAL          | Service / DB / Upstream     |\n\n---\n\n## 5. REST Endpoints\n\n### 5.1 Ledger Entries\n\n#### 5.1.1 List Entries\n```\nGET /v1/ledgers/entries\n```\n\nQuery parameters:\n\n| Name          | Type   | Description                                    |\n|---------------|--------|------------------------------------------------|\n| `account_id`  | UUID   | Filter by account                              |\n| `from_date`   | date   | Inclusive start (ISO-8601)                     |\n| `to_date`     | date   | Inclusive end (ISO-8601)                       |\n| `page[size]`  | int    | Items per page (default: 100, max: 1000)       |\n| `page[cursor]`| string | Cursor returned by previous call               |\n\nExample:\n\n```bash\ncurl -H \"Accept: application/vnd.ledgerlink.v1+json\" \\\n     -H \"Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN\" \\\n     \"https://api.ledgerlink.io/v1/ledgers/entries?account_id=ef83914f-4b2b-4ea5-9d38-38d79f5e70bc&page[size]=50\"\n```\n\nSuccessful response (`200 OK`):\n\n```json\n{\n  \"data\": [\n    {\n      \"entry_id\": \"2e862563-37f7-4b9e-a55b-5f55fb8028b8\",\n      \"account_id\": \"ef83914f-4b2b-4ea5-9d38-38d79f5e70bc\",\n      \"amount\": 1542.25,\n      \"currency\": \"USD\",\n      \"direction\": \"DEBIT\",\n      \"posting_date\": \"2024-04-30\",\n      \"description\": \"Invoice 45602\",\n      \"external_ref\": \"ERP#45602\",\n      \"created_at\": \"2024-04-30T12:34:42.125Z\",\n      \"updated_at\": \"2024-04-30T12:34:42.125Z\"\n    }\n    // ...\n  ],\n  \"meta\": {\n    \"page\": {\n      \"has_next\": true,\n      \"next_cursor\": \"g3QAAAACZAACaWRtAAAAPGU4\"\n    },\n    \"cache\": {\n      \"etag\": \"W/\\\"67d32bca9\\\"\",\n      \"max_age_seconds\": 30\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\nServers MAY return the `ETag` header. Supplying `If-None-Match` will trigger a `304 Not Modified`.\n\n#### 5.1.2 Create Entry\n```\nPOST /v1/ledgers/entries\nContent-Type: application/json\n```\n\n```json\n{\n  \"account_id\": \"ef83914f-4b2b-4ea5-9d38-38d79f5e70bc\",\n  \"amount\": 1542.25,\n  \"currency\": \"USD\",\n  \"direction\": \"DEBIT\",\n  \"posting_date\": \"2024-04-30\",\n  \"description\": \"Invoice 45602\",\n  \"external_ref\": \"ERP#45602\"\n}\n```\n\nValidation rules enforced by the View-Model:\n\n* `amount > 0`\n* `currency` conforms to ISO 4217\n* `posting_date` \u2264 current date\n* `external_ref` \u2264 100 characters (UTF-8)\n\nOn success (`201 Created`) the response body matches GET by ID.\n\n#### 5.1.3 Retrieve Entry\n```\nGET /v1/ledgers/entries/{entry_id}\n```\n\nReturns `404 Not Found` when the entry does not exist or tenant mismatch.\n\n#### 5.1.4 Update Entry\n```\nPATCH /v1/ledgers/entries/{entry_id}\nContent-Type: application/merge-patch+json\n```\n\nImmutable fields (`entry_id`, `account_id`, `currency`, `direction`) are ignored with `412 Precondition Failed`.\n\n---\n\n### 5.2 Account Snapshots\n\n```\nGET /v1/accounts/{account_id}/snapshots\n```\n\nSnapshots collapse entries into daily balances.\n\n| Query Param | Description                         |\n|-------------|-------------------------------------|\n| `from_date` | Inclusive start date (ISO-8601)     |\n| `to_date`   | Inclusive end date   (ISO-8601)     |\n\n```json\n{\n  \"data\": [\n    {\n      \"as_of\": \"2024-04-30\",\n      \"balance\": 78542.91,\n      \"currency\": \"USD\"\n    }\n  ],\n  \"meta\": {\n    \"generated_at\": \"2024-04-30T23:59:59Z\"\n  }\n}\n```\n\nSnapshots are cached aggressively (TTL = 300s) and revalidated on ledger mutations.\n\n---\n\n### 5.3 Cash-Flow Forecasts\n\n```\nPOST /v1/cashflows/forecasts\n```\n\nRequest body:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"account_ids\": [\"ef83914f-4b2b-4ea5-9d38-38d79f5e70bc\"],\n  \"horizon_days\": 90,\n  \"scenario\": \"BASELINE\"\n}\n```\n\nResponse (`202 Accepted`) returns a `forecast_id` and begins async processing.  \nPoll status:\n\n```\nGET /v1/cashflows/forecasts/{forecast_id}\n```\n\nPossible `status` values: `PENDING`, `IN_PROGRESS`, `READY`, `FAILED`.\n\n---\n\n## 6. GraphQL Endpoint\n\n```\nPOST /graphql\nContent-Type: application/json\n```\n\n### 6.1 Schema Snapshot (excerpt)\n\n```graphql\ntype LedgerEntry {\n  entryId: UUID!\n  accountId: UUID!\n  amount: Decimal!\n  currency: Currency!\n  direction: Direction!\n  postingDate: Date!\n  description: String\n  externalRef: String\n  createdAt: DateTime!\n  updatedAt: DateTime!\n}\n\ntype Query {\n  ledgerEntries(\n    accountId: UUID\n    fromDate: Date\n    toDate: Date\n    after: String\n    first: Int = 100\n  ): LedgerEntryConnection!\n}\n\ntype Mutation {\n  createLedgerEntry(input: CreateLedgerEntryInput!): LedgerEntry!\n  updateLedgerEntry(entryId: UUID!, patch: UpdateLedgerEntryPatch!): LedgerEntry!\n}\n```\n\n### 6.2 Example Query\n\n```graphql\nquery Entries($account: UUID!, $cursor: String) {\n  ledgerEntries(accountId: $account, first: 50, after: $cursor) {\n    nodes {\n      entryId\n      amount\n      currency\n      postingDate\n    }\n    pageInfo {\n      hasNextPage\n      endCursor\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 7. Pagination & Caching\nNexus employs _cursor-based pagination_ (`page[cursor]`). Cursors are opaque Base64-encoded and signed.\n\nResponses MAY include:\n\n```\nCache-Control: private, max-age=30, stale-while-revalidate=30\nETag: W/\"67d32bca9\"\n```\n\nClients SHOULD provide `If-None-Match` for cache hits and store cursors per filter signature.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Rate Limiting\nDefault production limits:\n\n| Resource            | Limit                       |\n|---------------------|-----------------------------|\n| **Authenticated**   | 600 requests / minute / key |\n| **Unauthenticated** | *Not supported*             |\n\nHeaders:\n\n```\nX-RateLimit-Limit: 600\nX-RateLimit-Remaining: 587\nX-RateLimit-Reset: 1714928420\n```\n\nExceeding returns `429 Too Many Requests` with a `Retry-After` header.\n\n---\n\n## 9. Observability & Tracing\nAll requests must include a UUID4 `X-Correlation-Id` header; otherwise the gateway assigns one.\n\nStructured logs are emitted in the [OpenTelemetry](https://opentelemetry.io/) semantic conventions and shipped to the **LogDNA** cluster.  \nTracing: W3C `traceparent` header is honored.\n\n---\n\n## 10. Changelog\n\n### 1.4.0 \u2013 2024-05-01\n* Added `direction` field enum values validation.\n* Introduced async forecast processing with `/cashflows/forecasts`.\n\n### 1.3.0 \u2013 2024-03-26\n* Experimental GraphQL endpoint (`/graphql`) graduated to GA.\n\n### 1.2.2 \u2013 2024-02-14\n* Improved pagination performance with Redis cursor cache.\n\n---\n\n_For questions, contact dev-support@ledgerlink.io or join our Slack community._  \n```",

In a real code-base it would live in `src/ledger_entry.rs`.\n\nuse std::sync::Arc;\n\nuse async_trait::async_trait;\nuse chrono::{DateTime, Utc};\nuse redis::AsyncCommands;\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse sqlx::{postgres::PgPoolOptions, PgPool, Row};\nuse thiserror::Error;\nuse tokio::sync::RwLock;\nuse tracing::{instrument, Instrument};\n\n/// Max number of records the API will ever return in a single call.\n/// Acts as a safeguard against pathological requests.\nconst HARD_PAGE_SIZE_LIMIT: u16 = 1_000;\n\n/// Domain object representing an immutable entry in the ledger.\n///\n/// NOTE: The table uses `NUMERIC(38, 10)` for `amount` in Postgres but we\n/// materialise it as `rust_decimal::Decimal` to maintain precision.\n#[derive(Clone, Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct LedgerEntry {\n    pub id: i64,\n    pub tenant_id: i64,\n    pub account_id: i64,\n    pub amount: rust_decimal::Decimal,\n    pub currency: String,\n    pub booked_at: DateTime<Utc>,\n    pub memo: Option<String>,\n}\n\n/// View-model that the REST/GraphQL layer consumes.\n/// It is purposely flattened to hide internal IDs.\n#[derive(Clone, Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct LedgerEntryDto {\n    pub uuid: String,\n    pub amount: rust_decimal::Decimal,\n    pub currency: String,\n    pub booked_at: DateTime<Utc>,\n    pub memo: Option<String>,\n}\n\nimpl From<LedgerEntry> for LedgerEntryDto {\n    fn from(e: LedgerEntry) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            uuid: base62::encode(e.id as u128),\n            amount: e.amount,\n            currency: e.currency,\n            booked_at: e.booked_at,\n            memo: e.memo,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Pagination request coming from the API.\n///\n/// `page` is 1-based because it is more ergonomic for clients.\n#[derive(Clone, Copy, Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct PageRequest {\n    pub page: u32,\n    pub per_page: u16,\n}\n\nimpl PageRequest {\n    /// Sanitises caller input: caps `per_page` and guarantees `page >= 1`.\n    pub fn sanitise(self) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            page: self.page.max(1),\n            per_page: self.per_page.min(HARD_PAGE_SIZE_LIMIT).max(1),\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Calculates SQL offset.\n    pub fn offset(&self) -> i64 {\n        ((self.page - 1) * self.per_page as u32) as i64\n    }\n}\n\n/// Structured page response returned to the API layer.\n#[derive(Clone, Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct Page<T> {\n    pub data: Vec<T>,\n    pub next_page: Option<u32>,\n    pub total: Option<u64>,\n}\n\n/// Shared error type for repository/service-level failures.\n#[derive(Error, Debug)]\npub enum LedgerError {\n    #[error(\"database error: {0}\")]\n    Db(#[from] sqlx::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"redis error: {0}\")]\n    Cache(#[from] redis::RedisError),\n\n    #[error(\"ledger entry not found\")]\n    NotFound,\n\n    #[error(\"invalid state: {0}\")]\n    InvalidState(String),\n}\n\npub type Result<T> = std::result::Result<T, LedgerError>;\n\n/// Abstraction hiding persistent storage semantics.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait LedgerEntryRepository: Send + Sync {\n    async fn insert(&self, entry: &LedgerEntry) -> Result<i64>;\n    async fn get(&self, tenant_id: i64, entry_id: i64) -> Result<LedgerEntry>;\n    async fn fetch_page(\n        &self,\n        tenant_id: i64,\n        req: PageRequest,\n    ) -> Result<(Vec<LedgerEntry>, u64)>;\n}\n\n/// PostgreSQL implementation backed by sqlx.\n/// This concrete type is not exposed outside this module.\npub struct PostgresLedgerEntryRepo {\n    pool: PgPool,\n}\n\nimpl PostgresLedgerEntryRepo {\n    pub async fn new(database_url: &str, max_connections: u32) -> Result<Self> {\n        let pool = PgPoolOptions::new()\n            .max_connections(max_connections)\n            .connect(database_url)\n            .await\n            .map_err(LedgerError::Db)?;\n\n        Ok(Self { pool })\n    }\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl LedgerEntryRepository for PostgresLedgerEntryRepo {\n    #[instrument(skip(self, entry), level = \"debug\")]\n    async fn insert(&self, entry: &LedgerEntry) -> Result<i64> {\n        let rec = sqlx::query(\n            r#\"\n            INSERT INTO ledger_entries\n                    (tenant_id, account_id, amount, currency, booked_at, memo)\n            VALUES  ($1,        $2,         $3,     $4,       $5,        $6)\n            RETURNING id;\n        \"#,\n        )\n        .bind(entry.tenant_id)\n        .bind(entry.account_id)\n        .bind(entry.amount)\n        .bind(&entry.currency)\n        .bind(entry.booked_at)\n        .bind(&entry.memo)\n        .fetch_one(&self.pool)\n        .await?;\n\n        Ok(rec.get::<i64, _>(\"id\"))\n    }\n\n    #[instrument(skip(self), level = \"trace\")]\n    async fn get(&self, tenant_id: i64, entry_id: i64) -> Result<LedgerEntry> {\n        let rec = sqlx::query_as!(\n            LedgerEntry,\n            r#\"\n            SELECT id, tenant_id, account_id, amount, currency, booked_at, memo\n            FROM   ledger_entries\n            WHERE  tenant_id = $1 AND id = $2\n        \"#,\n            tenant_id,\n            entry_id\n        )\n        .fetch_optional(&self.pool)\n        .await?\n        .ok_or(LedgerError::NotFound)?;\n\n        Ok(rec)\n    }\n\n    #[instrument(skip(self), level = \"debug\")]\n    async fn fetch_page(\n        &self,\n        tenant_id: i64,\n        req: PageRequest,\n    ) -> Result<(Vec<LedgerEntry>, u64)> {\n        // 1. Count total for the tenant.\n        let total: (i64,) = sqlx::query_as(\n            r#\"SELECT COUNT(*) as count FROM ledger_entries WHERE tenant_id = $1\"#,\n        )\n        .bind(tenant_id)\n        .fetch_one(&self.pool)\n        .await?;\n\n        // 2. Fetch requested slice.\n        let rows = sqlx::query_as!(\n            LedgerEntry,\n            r#\"\n            SELECT id, tenant_id, account_id, amount, currency, booked_at, memo\n            FROM   ledger_entries\n            WHERE  tenant_id = $1\n            ORDER  BY booked_at DESC, id DESC\n            OFFSET $2 LIMIT $3\n        \"#,\n            tenant_id,\n            req.offset(),\n            req.per_page as i64\n        )\n        .fetch_all(&self.pool)\n        .await?;\n\n        Ok((rows, total.0 as u64))\n    }\n}\n\n/// High-level service orchestrating repository and distributed cache.\n///\n/// Caches individual `LedgerEntryDto` objects to minimise DB traffic for\n/// idempotent GET requests. The caching strategy is a simple \u201ccache-aside\u201d\n/// with a 10 minute TTL. We purposely keep the implementation thin; in real\n/// life we would centralise this logic through a reusable Redis wrapper.\n#[derive(Clone)]\npub struct LedgerEntryService<R: LedgerEntryRepository> {\n    repo: Arc<R>,\n    redis: redis::Client,\n    // Small in-memory cache to ameliorate thundering herd during short periods.\n    in_memory: Arc<RwLock<lru::LruCache<i64, LedgerEntryDto>>>,\n}\n\nimpl<R: LedgerEntryRepository> LedgerEntryService<R> {\n    pub fn new(repo: R, redis_url: &str, mem_cache_cap: usize) -> Result<Self> {\n        Ok(Self {\n            repo: Arc::new(repo),\n            redis: redis::Client::open(redis_url).map_err(LedgerError::Cache)?,\n            in_memory: Arc::new(RwLock::new(lru::LruCache::new(\n                mem_cache_cap.try_into().unwrap_or(256),\n            ))),\n        })\n    }\n\n    fn redis_key(tenant_id: i64, entry_id: i64) -> String {\n        format!(\"tenant:{tenant_id}:ledger_entry:{entry_id}\")\n    }\n\n    /// Inserts a new entry and invalidates affected caches.\n    #[instrument(skip(self, entry), level = \"info\")]\n    pub async fn create_entry(&self, entry: &LedgerEntry) -> Result<i64> {\n        // Basic validation rule: amount cannot be 0.\n        if entry.amount.is_zero() {\n            return Err(LedgerError::InvalidState(\n                \"Amount cannot be zero\".to_string(),\n            ));\n        }\n\n        let id = self.repo.insert(entry).await?;\n\n        // Invalidate parent list (simple strategy: delete entire key space).\n        let mut conn = self.redis.get_async_connection().await?;\n        let pattern = format!(\"tenant:{}:ledger_entry:*\", entry.tenant_id);\n        let _: () = redis::cmd(\"UNLINK\").arg(pattern).query_async(&mut conn).await?;\n\n        // Evict in-memory cache.\n        self.in_memory.write().await.pop(&id);\n\n        Ok(id)\n    }\n\n    /// Fetches a single entry, going through L1 (memory) & L2 (Redis) caches.\n    #[instrument(skip(self), level = \"debug\")]\n    pub async fn get_entry(\n        &self,\n        tenant_id: i64,\n        entry_id: i64,\n    ) -> Result<LedgerEntryDto> {\n        // 1. Check L1.\n        if let Some(dto) = self.in_memory.read().await.get(&entry_id).cloned() {\n            return Ok(dto);\n        }\n\n        // 2. Check Redis.\n        let redis_key = Self::redis_key(tenant_id, entry_id);\n        let mut conn = self.redis.get_async_connection().await?;\n        if let Ok(Some(binary)) = conn.get::<_, Vec<u8>>(&redis_key).await {\n            let dto: LedgerEntryDto = bincode::deserialize(&binary)\n                .map_err(|e| LedgerError::InvalidState(e.to_string()))?;\n            // Fill L1.\n            self.in_memory.write().await.put(entry_id, dto.clone());\n            return Ok(dto);\n        }\n\n        // 3. Fallback to DB.\n        let entry = self.repo.get(tenant_id, entry_id).await?;\n        let dto = LedgerEntryDto::from(entry.clone());\n\n        // Back-fill caches.\n        let _: () = conn\n            .set_ex(\n                &redis_key,\n                bincode::serialize(&dto).unwrap(),\n                600, // seconds\n            )\n            .await?;\n        self.in_memory.write().await.put(entry_id, dto.clone());\n\n        Ok(dto)\n    }\n\n    /// Retrieves a paginated list, with optional total count.\n    #[instrument(skip(self), level = \"debug\")]\n    pub async fn list_entries(\n        &self,\n        tenant_id: i64,\n        req: PageRequest,\n    ) -> Result<Page<LedgerEntryDto>> {\n        let req = req.sanitise();\n        // At scale we would paginated-cache \u201cpages\u201d too, but omit for brevity.\n        let (rows, total) = self.repo.fetch_page(tenant_id, req).await?;\n        let data: Vec<LedgerEntryDto> = rows.into_iter().map(Into::into).collect();\n\n        let consumed = (req.page as u64) * (req.per_page as u64);\n        let next_page = if consumed < total {\n            Some(req.page + 1)\n        } else {\n            None\n        };\n\n        Ok(Page {\n            data,\n            next_page,\n            total: Some(total),\n        })\n    }\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n    use rust_decimal_macros::dec;\n    use serial_test::serial;\n\n    // Helper to build an in-memory postgres (requires `cargo test -- --ignored`\n    // if dockerised). Kept minimal for brevity.\n    async fn bootstrap_repo() -> PostgresLedgerEntryRepo {\n        let db_url =\n            std::env::var(\"TEST_DATABASE_URL\").expect(\"Set TEST_DATABASE_URL\");\n        let repo = PostgresLedgerEntryRepo::new(&db_url, 5)\n            .await\n            .expect(\"failed to init repo\");\n\n        // Initialise schema (idempotent).\n        sqlx::migrate!().run(&repo.pool).await.unwrap();\n\n        repo\n    }\n\n    #[tokio::test]\n    #[serial] // Avoid test inter-dependency on the DB.\n    async fn crud_roundtrip() {\n        let repo = bootstrap_repo().await;\n        let svc =\n            LedgerEntryService::new(repo, \"redis://127.0.0.1/\", 128).unwrap();\n\n        let entry = LedgerEntry {\n            id: 0,\n            tenant_id: 42,\n            account_id: 100,\n            amount: dec!(123.45),\n            currency: \"USD\".into(),\n            booked_at: Utc::now(),\n            memo: Some(\"integration test\".into()),\n        };\n\n        let id = svc.create_entry(&entry).await.unwrap();\n        assert!(id > 0);\n\n        let dto1 = svc.get_entry(42, id).await.unwrap();\n        let dto2 = svc.get_entry(42, id).await.unwrap(); // should hit cache\n\n        assert_eq!(dto1.amount, dto2.amount);\n\n        let page = svc\n            .list_entries(\n                42,\n                PageRequest {\n                    page: 1,\n                    per_page: 10,\n                },\n            )\n            .await\n            .unwrap();\n        assert_eq!(page.data.len(), 1);\n    }\n}\n```",

.get(\"offset\")\n            .and_then(|v| v.parse::<u32>().ok())\n            .unwrap_or_default();\n\n        let limit = params\n            .get(\"limit\")\n            .and_then(|v|     "content": "```rust\n//! src/module_46.rs\n//!\n//! Pagination-aware, type-safe Redis cache for \u201cQuery\u201d side of the\n//! Command/Query separation used by LedgerLink Nexus.  The cache is designed\n//! to work in a multi-tenant, horizontally-scaled micro-service and therefore\n//! supports:\n//!   \u2022 namespaced keys (tenant isolation)\n//!   \u2022 expirations / soft TTL\n//!   \u2022 pub/sub-based fan-out invalidation\n//!   \u2022 structured tracing and metrics\n//!\n//! The public API intentionally mimics an ordinary repository call so the\n//! surrounding service layer can stay oblivious to the actual caching\n//! strategy.\n//!\n//! # Example\n//! ```no_run\n//! # use uuid::Uuid;\n//! # use ledgerlink_nexus::cache::{PagedCache, Pagination, CacheableQuery};\n//! # use tokio::runtime::Runtime;\n//! #\n//! #[derive(Clone, Debug)]\n//! struct GetLedgerEntryPage {\n//!     pub tenant_id: Uuid,\n//!     pub account_id: Uuid,\n//!     pub pagination: Pagination,\n//! }\n//!\n//! impl CacheableQuery for GetLedgerEntryPage {\n//!     fn tenant_id(&self) -> Uuid { self.tenant_id }\n//!     fn pagination(&self) -> &Pagination { &self.pagination }\n//!     fn cache_hash(&self) -> String {\n//!         format!(\"account:{}\", self.account_id)\n//!     }\n//! }\n//!\n//! # Runtime::new().unwrap().block_on(async move {\n//! let redis_url = \"redis://127.0.0.1/\";\n//! let cache = PagedCache::<serde_json::Value>::connect(redis_url)\n//!     .await\n//!     .expect(\"redis must be up\");\n//!\n//! let query = GetLedgerEntryPage {\n//!     tenant_id: Uuid::new_v4(),\n//!     account_id: Uuid::new_v4(),\n//!     pagination: Pagination::new(0, 50).unwrap(),\n//! };\n//!\n//! let (_v, from_cache) = cache\n//!     .get_or_query(&query, || async {\n//!         // .. expensive DB call here ..\n//!         Ok(serde_json::json!({\"dummy\": true }))\n//!     })\n//!     .await\n//!     .unwrap();\n//! # });\n//! ```\n\nuse std::time::Duration;\n\nuse async_trait::async_trait;\nuse bytes::Bytes;\nuse redis::{aio::ConnectionManager, AsyncCommands};\nuse serde::{de::DeserializeOwned, Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse thiserror::Error;\nuse tokio::{sync::broadcast, time};\nuse tracing::{debug, instrument, warn};\nuse uuid::Uuid;\n\n/// Hard upper-bound for `per_page` to protect Redis payload size and memory\n/// pressure.  A single cached page must never exceed this many items.\nconst MAX_PAGE_SIZE: usize = 250;\n\n/// Built-in soft time-to-live for cached pages.\n///\n/// Note: domain services may override this by providing\n/// `PagedCache::with_ttl`.\nconst DEFAULT_TTL: Duration = Duration::from_secs(30);\n\n/// Redis channel used for fan-out invalidation events.\nconst INVALIDATION_CHANNEL: &str = \"ledgerlink:nexus:cache:evict\";\n\n/// Common error envelope returned by this module.\n#[derive(Error, Debug)]\npub enum CacheError {\n    #[error(\"redis error: {0}\")]\n    Redis(#[from] redis::RedisError),\n    #[error(\"serialization error: {0}\")]\n    Bincode(#[from] bincode::Error),\n    #[error(\"application error: {0}\")]\n    Application(#[from] anyhow::Error),\n}\n\n/// Pagination information sent by a caller or deserialized from a request\n/// payload.  It purposely mirrors the GraphQL \u201cConnection\u201d spec as well as the\n/// REST flavour used in our OpenAPI contract.\n#[derive(Clone, Copy, Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct Pagination {\n    pub page: usize,\n    pub per_page: usize,\n}\n\nimpl Pagination {\n    /// Construct a new pagination config while enforcing invariants.\n    pub fn new(page: usize, per_page: usize) -> Result<Self, CacheError> {\n        if per_page == 0 || per_page > MAX_PAGE_SIZE {\n            anyhow::bail!(\n                \"per_page must be within 1..={MAX_PAGE_SIZE} (got {per_page})\"\n            );\n        }\n        Ok(Self { page, per_page })\n    }\n}\n\n/// Trait implemented by every Query object that wishes to leverage the cache.\n/// Only a handful of methods are required so the domain code remains\n/// decoupled from Redis.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait CacheableQuery: Send + Sync {\n    /// A tenant-scoped uuid allowing sharding and event fan-out.\n    fn tenant_id(&self) -> Uuid;\n\n    /// Pagination info (page number + page size)\n    fn pagination(&self) -> &Pagination;\n\n    /// Deterministic hash that uniquely identifies the query parameters\n    /// **excluding** pagination (e.g. account, date_range, filters).\n    ///\n    /// Think of this as a stable, human-readable identifier.\n    fn cache_hash(&self) -> String;\n}\n\n/// Envelope stored in Redis.  We prepend a short version tag so we can bump\n/// serialization format without flushing the whole store.\n#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\nstruct CachedEnvelope<T> {\n    v: u8,\n    data: T,\n}\n\n/// A concrete Redis-backed cache aware of pagination and invalidation events.\npub struct PagedCache<T> {\n    conn: ConnectionManager,\n    ttl: Duration,\n    /// Broadcast channel used locally for best-effort, in-process fan-out.\n    evict_tx: broadcast::Sender<String>,\n    _phantom: std::marker::PhantomData<T>,\n}\n\nimpl<T> PagedCache<T>\nwhere\n    T: Serialize + DeserializeOwned + Send + Sync + 'static,\n{\n    /// Connect to Redis and spawn a small background task listening for\n    /// invalidation events.\n    pub async fn connect(redis_url: &str) -> Result<Self, CacheError> {\n        let client = redis::Client::open(redis_url)?;\n        let manager = ConnectionManager::new(client).await?;\n        let (tx, _rx) = broadcast::channel(64);\n\n        // Spawn invalidation listener\n        Self::spawn_invalidator(redis_url.to_owned(), tx.clone());\n\n        Ok(Self {\n            conn: manager,\n            ttl: DEFAULT_TTL,\n            evict_tx: tx,\n            _phantom: std::marker::PhantomData,\n        })\n    }\n\n    /// Provide a custom TTL.  Fluent-style builder.\n    pub fn with_ttl(mut self, ttl: Duration) -> Self {\n        self.ttl = ttl;\n        self\n    }\n\n    /// Try to fetch from cache or execute `fetch_fn` and then cache the\n    /// outcome.  The second value in the tuple indicates whether it was\n    /// a cache hit.\n    #[instrument(skip_all, fields(cache.key = %self.derive_key(query)))]\n    pub async fn get_or_query<Q, F, E>(\n        &self,\n        query: &Q,\n        fetch_fn: F,\n    ) -> Result<(T, bool), CacheError>\n    where\n        Q: CacheableQuery,\n        F: std::future::Future<Output = Result<T, E>> + Send,\n        E: Into<anyhow::Error> + Send,\n    {\n        let redis_key = self.derive_key(query);\n        // 1. Optimistic local in-process check first\n        if let Ok(value) = self.try_get_local(&redis_key).await {\n            return Ok((value, true));\n        }\n\n        // 2. Grab from Redis\n        let mut conn = self.conn.clone();\n        if let Some(raw): Option<Vec<u8>> = conn.get(&redis_key).await? {\n            let envelope: CachedEnvelope<T> = bincode::deserialize(&raw)?;\n            // No versioning strategy yet, v=0\n            debug!(\"Cache hit (redis)\");\n            self.populate_local(redis_key.clone(), envelope.data.clone())\n                .await;\n            return Ok((envelope.data, true));\n        }\n\n        // 3. Miss \u2013 execute provided closure\n        debug!(\"Cache miss; delegating to fetch_fn\");\n        let fresh = fetch_fn.await.map_err(Into::into)?;\n\n        // 4. Save to Redis (fire-and-forget)\n        let save_redis_key = redis_key.clone();\n        let save_ttl = self.ttl;\n        let save_value = fresh.clone();\n        tokio::spawn(async move {\n            let env = CachedEnvelope { v: 0, data: save_value };\n            if let Ok(payload) = bincode::serialize(&env) {\n                let _: Result<(), _> = conn\n                    .set_ex(save_redis_key, payload, save_ttl.as_secs() as usize)\n                    .await;\n            }\n        });\n\n        // 5. Fill local cache\n        self.populate_local(redis_key, fresh.clone()).await;\n        Ok((fresh, false))\n    }\n\n    /// Explicitly evict a query result (all pages) for the given tenant/query\n    /// hash, broadcasting the event to every service instance.\n    ///\n    /// Should be called by the *Command* side whenever a mutation might\n    /// invalidate read models (e.g. posting a new ledger entry).\n    pub async fn evict<Q>(&self, query: &Q) -> Result<(), CacheError>\n    where\n        Q: CacheableQuery,\n    {\n        let pattern = format!(\"nexus:{}:{}:*\", query.tenant_id(), query.cache_hash());\n        let mut conn = self.conn.clone();\n        let _: () = redis::cmd(\"UNLINK\").arg(pattern.clone()).query_async(&mut conn).await?;\n\n        // Broadcast\n        let _ = conn.publish::<_, _, ()>(INVALIDATION_CHANNEL, pattern.clone()).await;\n        // Local channel\n        let _ = self.evict_tx.send(pattern);\n\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Assemble the final Redis key\n    fn derive_key<Q: CacheableQuery>(&self, query: &Q) -> String {\n        format!(\n            \"nexus:{}:{}:{}:{}\",\n            query.tenant_id(),\n            query.cache_hash(),\n            query.pagination().page,\n            query.pagination().per_page\n        )\n    }\n\n    // \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\n    // Local in-process cache (tiny, bounded, non-blocking)\n    // -------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n    async fn try_get_local(&self, k: &str) -> Result<T, CacheError> {\n        use moka::future::Cache;\n        static LOCAL: once_cell::sync::Lazy<Cache<String, Bytes>> =\n            once_cell::sync::Lazy::new(|| Cache::builder()\n                .max_capacity(4_096)\n                .time_to_live(DEFAULT_TTL)\n                .build());\n\n        if let Some(bytes) = LOCAL.get(k).await {\n            let env: CachedEnvelope<T> = bincode::deserialize(bytes.as_ref())?;\n            return Ok(env.data);\n        }\n        anyhow::bail!(\"not in local cache\")\n    }\n\n    async fn populate_local(&self, k: String, data: T) {\n        use moka::future::Cache;\n        static LOCAL: once_cell::sync::Lazy<Cache<String, Bytes>> =\n            once_cell::sync::Lazy::new(|| Cache::builder()\n                .max_capacity(4_096)\n                .time_to_live(DEFAULT_TTL)\n                .build());\n\n        if let Ok(payload) = bincode::serialize(&CachedEnvelope { v: 0, data }) {\n            let _ = LOCAL.insert(k, Bytes::from(payload)).await;\n        }\n    }\n\n    // \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\n    // Background Redis pub/sub listener \u2013 distribute invalidation events\n    // -------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n    fn spawn_invalidator(redis_url: String, evict_tx: broadcast::Sender<String>) {\n        tokio::spawn(async move {\n            loop {\n                match redis::Client::open(redis_url.as_str())\n                    .and_then(|c| c.get_async_connection())\n                    .await\n                {\n                    Ok(conn) => {\n                        if let Err(e) = Self::listen_invalidation(conn, evict_tx.clone()).await {\n                            warn!(error = %e, \"cache invalidation listener died; restarting\");\n                        };\n                    }\n                    Err(e) => {\n                        warn!(error = %e, \"cannot connect to redis for invalidation; retrying\");\n                        time::sleep(Duration::from_secs(5)).await;\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n        });\n    }\n\n    async fn listen_invalidation(\n        mut conn: redis::aio::Connection,\n        evict_tx: broadcast::Sender<String>,\n    ) -> Result<(), CacheError> {\n        use redis::AsyncCommands;\n\n        let mut pubsub = conn.as_pubsub();\n        pubsub.subscribe(INVALIDATION_CHANNEL).await?;\n\n        loop {\n            let msg = pubsub.on_message().await;\n            let payload: String = msg.get_payload()?;\n            // Re-emit into local broadcast\n            let _ = evict_tx.send(payload.clone());\n\n            // moka::future::Cache;\n        static LOCAL: once_cell::sync::Lazy<Cache<String, Bytes>> =\n            once_cell::sync::Lazy::new(|| Cache::builder()\n                .max_capacity(4_096)\n k.starts_with(pattern) {\n                LOCAL.invalidate(&k).await;\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n```",

This module is completely self-contained yet showcases the LedgerLink\n//! Nexus architecture principles:\n//!   \u2022 Clean separation between View (DTO)  \u279c  View-Model (validated\n//!     transport structs)  \u279c  Domain Models / Repository  \u279c  Service.\n//!   \u2022 Transparent response-caching with Redis using a typed cache key.\n//!   \u2022 Structured error handling with `thiserror` and `tracing`.\n//!   \u2022 Feature-gated compile options (`response_caching`) for optional\n//!     dependencies, keeping binary size and attack-surface minimal.\n//!\n//! Down-stream HTTP/GraphQL handlers can simply call\n//! `CashFlowForecastService::get_forecast(..)` and receive a fully\n//! validated, paginated & (optionally) cached payload ready to be\n//! serialized by the transport layer.\n\n#![allow(clippy::async_yields_async)] // False-positive for async_trait\n#![cfg_attr(docsrs, feature(doc_cfg))]\n\nuse std::{num::NonZeroU32, sync::Arc, time::Duration};\n\nuse async_trait::async_trait;\nuse chrono::{NaiveDate, Utc};\nuse rust_decimal::Decimal;\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse thiserror::Error;\nuse tokio::time::Instant;\nuse tracing::{debug, error, instrument, warn};\nuse uuid::Uuid;\n#[cfg(feature = \"response_caching\")]\nuse {\n    redis::{aio::ConnectionLike, AsyncCommands},\n    serde_json::json,\n};\n\n/// Inclusive date range used when querying forecasts.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct DateRange {\n    pub from: NaiveDate,\n    pub to: NaiveDate,\n}\n\nimpl DateRange {\n    pub fn validate(self) -> Result<Self, ValidationError> {\n        if self.from > self.to {\n            Err(ValidationError::InvalidDateRange)\n        } else {\n            Ok(self)\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Simple pagination descriptor (page & per_page are both 1-based).\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct Pagination {\n    page: NonZeroU32,\n    per_page: NonZeroU32,\n}\n\nimpl Pagination {\n    pub fn new(page: u32, per_page: u32) -> Result<Self, ValidationError> {\n        let page = NonZeroU32::new(page).ok_or(ValidationError::InvalidPage)?;\n        let per_page =\n            NonZeroU32::new(per_page).ok_or(ValidationError::InvalidPageSize)?;\n        Ok(Self { page, per_page })\n    }\n\n    #[inline]\n    pub fn offset(&self) -> u32 {\n        (self.page.get() - 1) * self.per_page.get()\n    }\n\n    #[inline]\n    pub fn limit(&self) -> u32 {\n        self.per_page.get()\n    }\n}\n\n/// Domain aggregate representing a single cash-flow forecast entry.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\npub struct CashFlowForecast {\n    pub id: Uuid,\n    pub account_id: Uuid,\n    pub date: NaiveDate,\n    pub expected_inflow: Decimal,\n    pub expected_outflow: Decimal,\n    pub currency: String,\n}\n\n/// Data Transfer Object returned to the outside world (View-Model).\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize)]\npub struct CashFlowForecastDto {\n    pub id: Uuid,\n    pub date: NaiveDate,\n    pub expected_inflow: Decimal,\n    pub expected_outflow: Decimal,\n    pub currency: String,\n}\n\nimpl From<CashFlowForecast> for CashFlowForecastDto {\n    fn from(f: CashFlowForecast) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            id: f.id,\n            date: f.date,\n            expected_inflow: f.expected_inflow,\n            expected_outflow: f.expected_outflow,\n            currency: f.currency,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Output envelope with pagination metadata.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize)]\npub struct CashFlowForecastPage {\n    pub items: Vec<CashFlowForecastDto>,\n    pub total_items: u64,\n    pub page: u32,\n    pub per_page: u32,\n}\n\n/// Domain-driven repository abstraction.\n///\n/// Implementations live in separate crates (e.g. `ledgerlink_pg`) and can\n/// be swapped at runtime using dependency-injection.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait CashFlowForecastRepository: Send + Sync + 'static {\n    async fn list_by_account(\n        &self,\n        account_id: Uuid,\n        range: DateRange,\n        pagination: Pagination,\n    ) -> Result<(Vec<CashFlowForecast>, u64), RepoError>;\n}\n\n/// Service fa\u00e7ade orchestrating query workflow.\npub struct CashFlowForecastService<R, C> {\n    repo: Arc<R>,\n    #[cfg(feature = \"response_caching\")]\n    cache: Arc<C>,\n    /// TTL for cache entries.\n    #[cfg(feature = \"response_caching\")]\n    ttl: Duration,\n}\n\nimpl<R, C> CashFlowForecastService<R, C>\nwhere\n    R: CashFlowForecastRepository,\n{\n    pub fn new(repo: Arc<R>) -> Self\n    where\n        C: Default,\n    {\n        Self {\n            repo,\n            #[cfg(feature = \"response_caching\")]\n            cache: Arc::<C>::default(),\n            #[cfg(feature = \"response_caching\")]\n            ttl: Duration::from_secs(300),\n        }\n    }\n\n    #[cfg_attr(\n        feature = \"response_caching\",\n        instrument(\n            name = \"CashFlowForecastService::get_forecast\",\n            skip(self),\n            fields(account_id = %account_id, page = pagination.page, per_page = pagination.per_page)\n        )\n    )]\n    #[cfg_attr(\n        not(feature = \"response_caching\"),\n        instrument(\n            name = \"CashFlowForecastService::get_forecast\",\n            skip(self),\n            fields(account_id = %account_id, page = pagination.page, per_page = pagination.per_page)\n        )\n    )]\n    pub async fn get_forecast(\n        &self,\n        account_id: Uuid,\n        range: DateRange,\n        pagination: Pagination,\n        force_refresh: bool,\n    ) -> Result<CashFlowForecastPage, ServiceError>\n    where\n        C: CacheBackend,\n    {\n        range.validate()?;\n\n        #[cfg(feature = \"response_caching\")]\n        if !force_refresh {\n            if let Some(cached) = self\n                .cache\n                .get::<CashFlowForecastPage>(&CacheKey::new(\n                    account_id,\n                    range,\n                    pagination,\n                ))\n                .await?\n            {\n                debug!(\"cache hit for account_id={}\", account_id);\n                return Ok(cached);\n            }\n        }\n\n        let span = tracing::info_span!(\"db_query\");\n        let _enter = span.enter();\n        let started_at = Instant::now();\n        let (rows, total) = self\n            .repo\n            .list_by_account(account_id, range, pagination)\n            .await\n            .map_err(ServiceError::Repository)?;\n        debug!(\"db_query completed in {:?}\", started_at.elapsed());\n\n        let page = CashFlowForecastPage {\n            items: rows.into_iter().map(Into::into).collect(),\n            total_items: total,\n            page: pagination.page.get(),\n            per_page: pagination.per_page.get(),\n        };\n\n        #[cfg(feature = \"response_caching\")]\n        {\n            self.cache\n                .set(\n                    CacheKey::new(account_id, range, pagination),\n                    &page,\n                    self.ttl,\n                )\n                .await?;\n        }\n\n        Ok(page)\n    }\n}\n\n//\n// ----------------------------- Caching ----------------------------------\n//\n#[cfg(feature = \"response_caching\")]\n#[async_trait]\npub trait CacheBackend: Send + Sync + 'static {\n    async fn get<T>(&self, key: &CacheKey) -> Result<Option<T>, CacheError>\n    where\n        T: for<'de> Deserialize<'de> + Send;\n    async fn set<T>(\n        &self,\n        key: CacheKey,\n        value: &T,\n        ttl: Duration,\n    ) -> Result<(), CacheError>\n    where\n        T: Serialize + Send + Sync;\n}\n\n/// Typed cache-key guaranteeing stable hash/serialize logic.\n#[cfg(feature = \"response_caching\")]\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Hash, PartialEq, Eq, Serialize)]\npub struct CacheKey {\n    account_id: Uuid,\n    from: NaiveDate,\n    to: NaiveDate,\n    page: u32,\n    per_page: u32,\n}\n\n#[cfg(feature = \"response_caching\")]\nimpl CacheKey {\n    pub fn new(\n        account_id: Uuid,\n        range: DateRange,\n        pagination: Pagination,\n    ) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            account_id,\n            from: range.from,\n            to: range.to,\n            page: pagination.page.get(),\n            per_page: pagination.per_page.get(),\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn as_redis_key(&self) -> String {\n        // Example key: cf_forecast:{acct}:{from}:{to}:{p}:{pp}\n        format!(\n            \"cf_forecast:{}:{}:{}:{}:{}\",\n            self.account_id, self.from, self.to, self.page, self.per_page\n        )\n    }\n}\n\n/// Minimal Redis cache backend implementation.\n#[cfg(all(feature = \"response_caching\", feature = \"redis\"))]\npub struct RedisCache<B: ConnectionLike + Send + Sync + 'static>(pub tokio::sync::Mutex<B>);\n\n#[cfg(all(feature = \"response_caching\", feature = \"redis\"))]\n#[async_trait]\nimpl<B> CacheBackend for RedisCache<B>\nwhere\n    B: ConnectionLike + Send + Sync + 'static,\n{\n    async fn get<T>(&self, key: &CacheKey) -> Result<Option<T>, CacheError>\n    where\n        T: for<'de> Deserialize<'de> + Send,\n    {\n        let redis_key = key.as_redis_key();\n        let mut conn = self.0.lock().await;\n        let data: Option<String> = conn.get(&redis_key).await?;\n        Ok(match data {\n            Some(s) => {\n                let parsed = serde_json::from_str::<T>(&s)?;\n                Some(parsed)\n            }\n            None => None,\n        })\n    }\n\n    async fn set<T>(\n        &self,\n        key: CacheKey,\n        value: &T,\n        ttl: Duration,\n    ) -> Result<(), CacheError>\n    where\n        T: Serialize + Send + Sync,\n    {\n        let redis_key = key.as_redis_key();\n        let payload = serde_json::to_string(value)?;\n        let mut conn = self.0.lock().await;\n        let _: () = conn\n            .set_ex::<_, _, ()>(&redis_key, payload, ttl.as_secs() as usize)\n            .await?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n//\n// ----------------------------- Errors -----------------------------------\n//\n\n#[derive(Debug, Error)]\npub enum ValidationError {\n    #[error(\"invalid pagination page (must be > 0)\")]\n    InvalidPage,\n    #[error(\"invalid page size (must be > 0)\")]\n    InvalidPageSize,\n    #[error(\"`from` date must be <= `to` date\")]\n    InvalidDateRange,\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Error)]\npub enum RepoError {\n    #[error(\"database error: {0}\")]\n    Db(#[from] anyhow::Error),\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Error)]\npub enum CacheError {\n    #[error(\"redis error: {0}\")]\n    Redis(#[from] redis::RedisError),\n    #[error(\"serialization error: {0}\")]\n    Serde(#[from] serde_json::Error),\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Error)]\npub enum ServiceError {\n    #[error(\"validation error: {0}\")]\n    Validation(#[from] ValidationError),\n    #[error(\"repository error: {0}\")]\n    Repository(#[from] RepoError),\n    #[cfg(feature = \"response_caching\")]\n    #[error(\"cache backend error: {0}\")]\n    Cache(#[from] CacheError),\n}\n\n//\n// ----------------------------- Tests
