  "content": "# Solution: rust_api_microservice_expert_008_architectural_understanding_expert_01\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThe LedgerLink Nexus service suffers from a **cache invalidation problem** where read handlers populate a Redis response cache on cache misses, but write handlers (POST/PUT/DELETE operations) **do not invalidate** or update the corresponding cache entries. This causes clients to receive stale data until the cache entry's TTL expires naturally.\n\n## Key Files Identified\n\n### Core Caching Modules\n- `/app/project/src/module_44.txt` - **Primary caching module**: High-volume Ledger Entry listing with Redis response-level caching. Contains `LedgerEntryQuerySvc` with `try_fetch_cache()` and `persist_cache()` methods, but only READ operations interact with cache.\n- `/app/project/src/module_46.txt` - **Pagination-aware Redis cache**: Contains `PagedCache<T>` with an explicit `evict()` method that *should* be called by write handlers but isn't wired to them.\n- `/app/project/src/module_33.txt` - **ResponseCache trait**: Defines cache abstraction with `invalidate()` method but write handlers don't use it.\n\n### Read Handler Modules (Query Side)\n- `/app/project/src/module_26.txt` - Ledger Entry Query Endpoint: Implements `get_ledger_entries()` handler that checks Redis cache before querying the database, stores results in cache on miss.\n- `/app/project/src/module_52.txt` - High-frequency paginated read-model for ledger entries with `LedgerEntryService::get_paginated()` that uses cache.\n- `/app/project/src/module_71.txt` - Cash-Flow Forecast query service with Redis-backed response caching.\n\n### Write Handler Modules (Command Side)\n- `/app/project/src/module_67.txt` - **Contains BOTH read and write operations**: Has `create_entry()` which properly invalidates cache (the exception), but this pattern is not replicated across other modules.\n- `/app/project/src/module_38.txt` - `LedgerEntryPgRepository::insert()` - Writes to database but has **NO cache invalidation**.\n\n### Configuration\n- `/app/project/src/config.txt` - Contains `ResponseCacheConfig` with `duration: Duration` (default 5 minutes TTL).\n- `/app/project/package.json` - Project manifest showing Rust-based microservice.\n- `/app/project/docs/api.md` - API documentation defining REST and GraphQL mutations.\n\n## Code Evidence\n\n### Evidence 1: Read Handler with Caching (module_44.txt)\n\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_44.txt\n// Lines: 355-408\n#[instrument(skip(self))]\npub async fn list(\n    &self,\n    tenant: Uuid,\n    query: ListQuery,\n) -> Result<Paginated<LedgerEntryDto>, ServiceError> {\n    // 1. Try cache (30ms timeout to avoid head-of-line blocking)\n    let key = Self::cache_key(tenant, &query);\n    if let Ok(Some(raw)) = self.try_fetch_cache(&key).await {\n        debug!(%tenant, %key, \"Cache hit\");\n        return serde_json::from_slice::<Paginated<LedgerEntryDto>>(&raw)\n            .map_err(ServiceError::CacheSerialization);\n    }\n\n    // 2. Query repository\n    debug!(%tenant, \"Cache miss \u2013 querying DB\");\n    let (entries, total) = self.repo.list(tenant, &query).await?;\n    // ... transforms entries ...\n\n    // 3. Backfill cache (best-effort)\n    let _ = self.persist_cache(&key, &payload).await;\n\n    Ok(payload)\n}\n\nasync fn persist_cache<T: Serialize>(&self, key: &str, value: &T) -> Result<(), ServiceError> {\n    let mut conn: RedisConn = self.redis.get().await?;\n    let data = serde_json::to_vec(value)?;\n    let _: () = conn\n        .set_ex(key, data, 60) // 60 seconds TTL\n        .await\n        .map_err(ServiceError::Cache)?;\n    Ok(())\n}\n```\n\n### Evidence 2: Write Handler WITHOUT Cache Invalidation (module_38.txt)\n\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_38.txt\n// Lines: 277-306\n/// An *idempotent* command that inserts a ledger entry inside its own\n/// transaction.  Exposed as a convenience; not part of the trait.\n///\n/// Demonstrates how we keep read & write paths separated (`CQRS` style).\nimpl LedgerEntryPgRepository {\n    #[instrument(skip_all, name = \"repo.ledger.insert\")]\n    pub async fn insert(&self, entry: &LedgerEntry) -> Result<(), PaginationError> {\n        let mut tx = self.pool.begin().await?;\n\n        sqlx::query(\n            r#\"\n            INSERT INTO ledger_entries\n            (id, account_id, amount, currency, description, created_at)\n            VALUES ($1, $2, $3, $4, $5, $6)\n            ON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING\n            \"#,\n        )\n        .bind(entry.id)\n        .bind(entry.account_id)\n        .bind(entry.amount)\n        .bind(&entry.currency)\n        .bind(&entry.description)\n        .bind(entry.created_at)\n        .execute(&mut tx)\n        .await?;\n\n        tx.commit().await?;\n        Ok(())\n        // NOTE: NO cache invalidation here!\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Evidence 3: Proper Cache Invalidation Pattern (module_67.txt)\n\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_67.txt\n// Lines: 251-272\n/// Inserts a new entry and invalidates affected caches.\n#[instrument(skip(self, entry), level = \"info\")]\npub async fn create_entry(&self, entry: &LedgerEntry) -> Result<i64> {\n    // Basic validation rule: amount cannot be 0.\n    if entry.amount.is_zero() {\n        return Err(LedgerError::InvalidState(\n            \"Amount cannot be zero\".to_string(),\n        ));\n    }\n\n    let id = self.repo.insert(entry).await?;\n\n    // Invalidate parent list (simple strategy: delete entire key space).\n    let mut conn = self.redis.get_async_connection().await?;\n    let pattern = format!(\"tenant:{}:ledger_entry:*\", entry.tenant_id);\n    let _: () = redis::cmd(\"UNLINK\").arg(pattern).query_async(&mut conn).await?;\n\n    // Evict in-memory cache.\n    self.in_memory.write().await.pop(&id);\n\n    Ok(id)\n}\n```\n\n### Evidence 4: Existing Cache Eviction Infrastructure (module_46.txt)\n\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_46.txt\n// Lines: 232-251\n/// Explicitly evict a query result (all pages) for the given tenant/query\n/// hash, broadcasting the event to every service instance.\n///\n/// Should be called by the *Command* side whenever a mutation might\n/// invalidate read models (e.g. posting a new ledger entry).\npub async fn evict<Q>(&self, query: &Q) -> Result<(), CacheError>\nwhere\n    Q: CacheableQuery,\n{\n    let pattern = format!(\"nexus:{}:{}:*\", query.tenant_id(), query.cache_hash());\n    let mut conn = self.conn.clone();\n    let _: () = redis::cmd(\"UNLINK\").arg(pattern.clone()).query_async(&mut conn).await?;\n\n    // Broadcast\n    let _ = conn.publish::<_, _, ()>(INVALIDATION_CHANNEL, pattern.clone()).await;\n    // Local channel\n    let _ = self.evict_tx.send(pattern);\n\n    Ok(())\n}\n```\n\n### Evidence 5: Cache Configuration (config.txt)\n\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/config.txt\n// Lines: 197-209\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\npub struct ResponseCacheConfig {\n    #[serde(default)]\n    pub enabled: bool,\n    #[serde(default = \"default_cache_duration\")]\n    pub duration: Duration,\n    #[serde(default)]\n    pub respect_cache_control_header: bool,\n}\n\nfn default_cache_duration() -> Duration {\n    Duration::from_secs(5 * 60) // 5 minutes\n}\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### How Components Interact\n\nThe LedgerLink Nexus system follows a CQRS (Command Query Responsibility Segregation) architecture pattern:\n\n1. **Read Path (Query Side)**:\n   - Client sends GET request \u2192 Handler (e.g., `module_44`, `module_26`, `module_52`)\n   - Handler checks Redis cache first using a computed cache key\n   - On cache hit: return cached response immediately\n   - On cache miss: query PostgreSQL repository, cache the result, return to client\n\n2. **Write Path (Command Side)**:\n   - Client sends POST/PUT/DELETE request \u2192 Write Handler (e.g., `module_38`, `module_71`)\n   - Handler persists changes to PostgreSQL\n   - **FLAW**: Handler does NOT invalidate or update the Redis cache\n   - Returns success to client\n\n3. **Cache Layer**:\n   - Redis serves as the primary caching backend\n   - Some modules (e.g., `module_67`) also use an in-memory LRU cache as L1\n   - Cache keys are composed of tenant_id + query parameters + pagination\n   - Default TTL is 5 minutes (300 seconds) for most entries, ranging from 15-60 seconds in various modules\n\n### The Architectural Flaw\n\n**The fundamental problem is the absence of an invalidation signal from write handlers to the cache layer.**\n\nWhen a write operation occurs:\n1. The database is updated successfully\n2. The cache still contains the old (stale) data\n3. Subsequent read requests hit the cache and return stale data\n4. Data only becomes consistent when the cache entry's TTL expires\n\nThis is a **classic cache coherence problem** in distributed systems. The codebase has the infrastructure to support cache invalidation (as seen in `module_46` with `PagedCache::evict()` and `module_67` with proper invalidation), but this pattern is not consistently applied across all write handlers.\n\n### Evidence of CQRS Design Intent\n\nThe code comments explicitly state the intent:\n- module_38.txt: \"Demonstrates how we keep read & write paths separated (`CQRS` style)\"\n- module_46.txt: \"Should be called by the *Command* side whenever a mutation might invalidate read models\"\n- module_33.txt: \"The cache is *write-through*: mutations trigger invalidations so we never serve stale financial data\"\n\nHowever, the implementation doesn't fulfill this contract\u2014most write handlers skip the invalidation step.\n\n## Solution Proposal\n\n### Design Pattern: Explicit Cache Invalidation\n\nThe recommended architectural solution is **Explicit Cache Invalidation** (also known as \"Cache-Aside with Manual Eviction\"). This pattern:\n\n1. Write handlers explicitly invalidate relevant cache entries after successful database writes\n2. Uses key pattern matching to invalidate all pages/variations of affected data\n3. Broadcasts invalidation events for distributed cache coherence\n\n### Why This Pattern?\n\n| Alternative | Pros | Cons | Decision |\n|-------------|------|------|----------|\n| **Explicit Invalidation** | Immediate consistency, targeted eviction, already partially implemented | Requires code changes in write handlers | **RECOMMENDED** |\n| Lower TTL | Simple to implement | Doesn't solve problem, just reduces window; hurts performance | NOT RECOMMENDED |\n| Write-through cache | Guarantees consistency | Higher write latency, complex to implement for paginated queries | OVERKILL |\n| Event-driven invalidation | Decoupled, scalable | Adds infrastructure complexity, eventual consistency | FOR FUTURE |\n\n### Justification\n\n1. **Immediate Consistency**: Financial data requires accurate, real-time reporting. Serving stale balances or ledger entries is unacceptable in B2B reconciliation.\n\n2. **Infrastructure Already Exists**: The `PagedCache::evict()` method in module_46 and the pattern in module_67 show the architecture already supports invalidation\u2014it just needs to be wired up.\n\n3. **Targeted Invalidation**: Using key patterns (e.g., `tenant:{id}:ledger_entry:*`) allows efficient bulk invalidation without flushing the entire cache.\n\n4. **Distributed Support**: The pub/sub mechanism in module_46 (`INVALIDATION_CHANNEL`) enables fan-out to all service instances in a horizontally-scaled deployment.\n\n## Implementation Plan\n\n### Modules Requiring Modification\n\n1. **Write Handler Modules** (must ADD cache invalidation calls):\n   - `module_38.txt` (LedgerEntryPgRepository::insert)\n   - `module_71.txt` (CashFlowForecastService - add mutation handlers)\n   - Any other modules with POST/PUT/DELETE handlers for ledger entries\n\n2. **Caching Modules** (may need enhancement):\n   - `module_44.txt` - Add `invalidate_tenant_entries()` method\n   - `module_46.txt` - Already has `evict()`, may need to be exposed more broadly\n   - `module_33.txt` - Ensure `invalidate()` method is accessible\n\n### New Interactions Required\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510      \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510      \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  Write Handler  \u2502 \u2500\u2500\u2500\u25ba \u2502  Database (PG)   \u2502      \u2502  Cache (Redis)  \u2502\n\u2502  (module_38)    \u2502      \u2502                  \u2502      \u2502                 \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518      \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518      \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u25b2\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n         \u2502                                                   \u2502\n         \u2502  2. After successful DB write,                   \u2502\n         \u2502     call cache.invalidate(key_pattern)           \u2502\n         \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n                         NEW INTERACTION\n```\n\n### Specific Changes\n\n**module_38.txt - Add cache invalidation to insert():**\n```rust\nimpl LedgerEntryPgRepository {\n    pub async fn insert(\n        &self,\n        entry: &LedgerEntry,\n        cache: &dyn CacheBackend  // NEW: inject cache dependency\n    ) -> Result<(), PaginationError> {\n        // ... existing database insert logic ...\n\n        tx.commit().await?;\n\n        // NEW: Invalidate cache after successful write\n        let pattern = format!(\"ledger_entries:{}:*\", entry.tenant_id);\n        cache.invalidate_pattern(&pattern).await?;\n\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**module_44.txt - Add invalidation method:**\n```rust\nimpl<R> LedgerEntryQuerySvc<R> {\n    /// Invalidate all cached entries for a tenant\n    pub async fn invalidate_tenant(&self, tenant: Uuid) -> Result<(), ServiceError> {\n        let pattern = format!(\"ledger_entries:{}:*\", tenant);\n        let mut conn = self.redis.get().await?;\n        let keys: Vec<String> = redis::cmd(\"KEYS\")\n            .arg(&pattern)\n            .query_async(&mut conn)\n            .await?;\n        if !keys.is_empty() {\n            redis::cmd(\"UNLINK\")\n                .arg(&keys)\n                .query_async(&mut conn)\n                .await?;\n        }\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**module_71.txt - Read operations cache responses in Redis, but write operations (POST/PUT/DELETE) do not invalidate the corresponding cache entries, causing clients to receive outdated data until TTL expiration.\n\n- **Key components**:\n  - Caching: `module_44`, `module_46`, `module_33`\n  - Read handlers: `module_26`, `module_52`, `module_71`\n  - Write handlers: `module_38`, `module_67`\n\n- **Architectural pattern**: The system uses CQRS (Command Query Responsibility Segregation) with a cache-aside pattern. The cache layer exists and has invalidation infrastructure (`PagedCache::evict()`, `ResponseCache::invalidate()`), but write handlers are not wired to call these methods.\n\n- **Root cause**: Write handlers in modules like `module_38` and most mutations do NOT call cache invalidation after successful database writes. The exception is `module_67::create_entry()` which properly invalidates cache\u2014this pattern needs to be replicated across all write handlers.\n\n- **Recommendations**:\n  1. Modify all write handlers (`module_38`, `module_71`, etc.) to call `cache.invalidate()` after successful DB writes\n  2. Use key pattern matching (e.g., `tenant:{id}:*`) for efficient bulk invalidation\n  3. Leverage existing pub/sub infrastructure (`INVALIDATION_CHANNEL`) for distributed cache coherence\n  4. Do NOT simply lower TTL\u2014this is ineffective for financial data consistency and hurts cache hit rates\n",

This causes clients to receive stale data until the cache entry's TTL expires naturally.\n\n## Key Files Identified\n\n### Core Caching Modules\n- `/app/project/src/module_44.txt` - **Primary caching module**: High-volume Ledger Entry listing with Redis response-level caching. Contains `LedgerEntryQuerySvc` with `try_fetch_cache()` and `persist_cache()` methods, but only READ operations interact with cache.\n- `/app/project/src/module_46.txt` - **Pagination-aware Redis cache**: Contains `PagedCache<T>` with an explicit `evict()` method that *should* be called by write handlers but isn't wired to them.\n- `/app/project/src/module_33.txt` - **ResponseCache trait**: Defines cache abstraction with `invalidate()` method but write handlers don't use it.\n\n### Read Handler Modules (Query Side)\n- `/app/project/src/module_26.txt` - Ledger Entry Query Endpoint: Implements `get_ledger_entries()` handler that checks Redis cache before querying the database, stores results in cache on miss.\n- `/app/project/src/module_52.txt` - High-frequency paginated read-model for ledger entries with `LedgerEntryService::get_paginated()` that uses cache.\n- `/app/project/src/module_71.txt` - Cash-Flow Forecast query service with Redis-backed response caching.\n\n### Write Handler Modules (Command Side)\n- `/app/project/src/module_67.txt` - **Contains BOTH read and write operations**: Has `create_entry()` which properly invalidates cache (the exception), but this pattern is not replicated across other modules.\n- `/app/project/src/module_38.txt` - `LedgerEntryPgRepository::insert()` - Writes to database but has **NO cache invalidation**.\n\n### Configuration\n- `/app/project/src/config.txt` - Contains `ResponseCacheConfig` with `duration: Duration` (default 5 minutes TTL).\n- `/app/project/package.json` - Project manifest showing Rust-based microservice.\n- `/app/project/docs/api.md` - API documentation defining REST and GraphQL mutations.\n\n## Code Evidence\n\n### Evidence 1: Read Handler with Caching (module_44.txt)\n\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_44.txt\n// Lines: 355-408\n#[instrument(skip(self))]\npub async fn list(\n    &self,\n    tenant: Uuid,\n    query: ListQuery,\n) -> Result<Paginated<LedgerEntryDto>, ServiceError> {\n    // 1. Try cache (30ms timeout to avoid head-of-line blocking)\n    let key = Self::cache_key(tenant, &query);\n    if let Ok(Some(raw)) = self.try_fetch_cache(&key).await {\n        debug!(%tenant, %key, \"Cache hit\");\n        return serde_json::from_slice::<Paginated<LedgerEntryDto>>(&raw)\n            .map_err(ServiceError::CacheSerialization);\n    }\n\n    // 2. Query repository\n    debug!(%tenant, \"Cache miss \u2013 querying DB\");\n    let (entries, total) = self.repo.list(tenant, &query).await?;\n    // ... transforms entries ...\n\n    // 3. Backfill cache (best-effort)\n    let _ = self.persist_cache(&key, &payload).await;\n\n    Ok(payload)\n}\n\nasync fn persist_cache<T: Serialize>(&self, key: &str, value: &T) -> Result<(), ServiceError> {\n    let mut conn: RedisConn = self.redis.get().await?;\n    let data = serde_json::to_vec(value)?;\n    let _: () = conn\n        .set_ex(key, data, 60) // 60 seconds TTL\n        .await\n        .map_err(ServiceError::Cache)?;\n    Ok(())\n}\n```\n\n### Evidence 2: Write Handler WITHOUT Cache Invalidation (module_38.txt)\n\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_38.txt\n// Lines: 277-306\n/// An *idempotent* command that inserts a ledger entry inside its own\n/// transaction.  Exposed as a convenience; not part of the trait.\n///\n/// Demonstrates how we keep read & write paths separated (`CQRS` style).\nimpl LedgerEntryPgRepository {\n    #[instrument(skip_all, name = \"repo.ledger.insert\")]\n    pub async fn insert(&self, entry: &LedgerEntry) -> Result<(), PaginationError> {\n        let mut tx = self.pool.begin().await?;\n\n        sqlx::query(\n            r#\"\n            INSERT INTO ledger_entries\n            (id, account_id, amount, currency, description, created_at)\n            VALUES ($1, $2, $3, $4, $5, $6)\n            ON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING\n            \"#,\n        )\n        .bind(entry.id)\n        .bind(entry.account_id)\n        .bind(entry.amount)\n        .bind(&entry.currency)\n        .bind(&entry.description)\n        .bind(entry.created_at)\n        .execute(&mut tx)\n        .await?;\n\n        tx.commit().await?;\n        Ok(())\n        // NOTE: NO cache invalidation here!\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Evidence 3: Proper Cache Invalidation Pattern (module_67.txt)\n\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_67.txt\n// Lines: 251-272\n/// Inserts a new entry and invalidates affected caches.\n#[instrument(skip(self, entry), level = \"info\")]\npub async fn create_entry(&self, entry: &LedgerEntry) -> Result<i64> {\n    // Basic validation rule: amount cannot be 0.\n    if entry.amount.is_zero() {\n        return Err(LedgerError::InvalidState(\n            \"Amount cannot be zero\".to_string(),\n        ));\n    }\n\n    let id = self.repo.insert(entry).await?;\n\n    // Invalidate parent list (simple strategy: delete entire key space).\n    let mut conn = self.redis.get_async_connection().await?;\n    let pattern = format!(\"tenant:{}:ledger_entry:*\", entry.tenant_id);\n    let _: () = redis::cmd(\"UNLINK\").arg(pattern).query_async(&mut conn).await?;\n\n    // Evict in-memory cache.\n    self.in_memory.write().await.pop(&id);\n\n    Ok(id)\n}\n```\n\n### Evidence 4: Existing Cache Eviction Infrastructure (module_46.txt)\n\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_46.txt\n// Lines: 232-251\n/// Explicitly evict a query result (all pages) for the given tenant/query\n/// hash, broadcasting the event to every service instance.\n///\n/// Should be called by the *Command* side whenever a mutation might\n/// invalidate read models (e.g. posting a new ledger entry).\npub async fn evict<Q>(&self, query: &Q) -> Result<(), CacheError>\nwhere\n    Q: CacheableQuery,\n{\n    let pattern = format!(\"nexus:{}:{}:*\", query.tenant_id(), query.cache_hash());\n    let mut conn = self.conn.clone();\n    let _: () = redis::cmd(\"UNLINK\").arg(pattern.clone()).query_async(&mut conn).await?;\n\n    // Broadcast\n    let _ = conn.publish::<_, _, ()>(INVALIDATION_CHANNEL, pattern.clone()).await;\n    // Local channel\n    let _ = self.evict_tx.send(pattern);\n\n    Ok(())\n}\n```\n\n### Evidence 5: Cache Configuration (config.txt)\n\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/config.txt\n// Lines: 197-209\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\npub struct ResponseCacheConfig {\n    #[serde(default)]\n    pub enabled: bool,\n    #[serde(default = \"default_cache_duration\")]\n    pub duration: Duration,\n    #[serde(default)]\n    pub respect_cache_control_header: bool,\n}\n\nfn default_cache_duration() -> Duration {\n    Duration::from_secs(5 * 60) // 5 minutes\n}\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### How Components Interact\n\nThe LedgerLink Nexus system follows a CQRS (Command Query Responsibility Segregation) architecture pattern:\n\n1. **Read Path (Query Side)**:\n   - Client sends GET request \u2192 Handler (e.g., `module_44`, `module_26`, `module_52`)\n   - Handler checks Redis cache first using a computed cache key\n   - On cache hit: return cached response immediately\n   - On cache miss: query PostgreSQL repository, cache the result, return to client\n\n2. **Write Path (Command Side)**:\n   - Client sends POST/PUT/DELETE request \u2192 Write Handler (e.g., `module_38`, `module_71`)\n   - Handler persists changes to PostgreSQL\n   - **FLAW**: Handler does NOT invalidate or update the Redis cache\n   - Returns success to client\n\n3. **Cache Layer**:\n   - Redis serves as the primary caching backend\n   - Some modules (e.g., `module_67`) also use an in-memory LRU cache as L1\n   - Cache keys are composed of tenant_id + query parameters + pagination\n   - Default TTL is 5 minutes (300 seconds) for most entries, ranging from 15-60 seconds in various modules\n\n### The Architectural Flaw\n\n**The fundamental problem is the absence of an invalidation signal from write handlers to the cache layer.**\n\nWhen a write operation occurs:\n1. The database is updated successfully\n2. The cache still contains the old (stale) data\n3. Subsequent read requests hit the cache and return stale data\n4. Data only becomes consistent when the cache entry's TTL expires\n\nThis is a **classic cache coherence problem** in distributed systems. The codebase has the infrastructure to support cache invalidation (as seen in `module_46` with `PagedCache::evict()` and `module_67` with proper invalidation), but this pattern is not consistently applied across all write handlers.\n\n### Evidence of CQRS Design Intent\n\nThe code comments explicitly state the intent:\n- module_38.txt: \"Demonstrates how we keep read & write paths separated (`CQRS` style)\"\n- module_46.txt: \"Should be called by the *Command* side whenever a mutation might invalidate read models\"\n- module_33.txt: \"The cache is *write-through*: mutations trigger invalidations so we never serve stale financial data\"\n\nHowever, the implementation doesn't fulfill this contract\u2014most write handlers skip the invalidation step.\n\n## Solution Proposal\n\n### Design Pattern: Explicit Cache Invalidation\n\nThe recommended architectural solution is **Explicit Cache Invalidation** (also known as \"Cache-Aside with Manual Eviction\"). This pattern:\n\n1. Write handlers explicitly invalidate relevant cache entries after successful database writes\n2. Uses key pattern matching to invalidate all pages/variations of affected data\n3. Broadcasts invalidation events for distributed cache coherence\n\n### Why This Pattern?\n\n| Alternative | Pros | Cons | Decision |\n|-------------|------|------|----------|\n| **Explicit Invalidation** | Immediate consistency, targeted eviction, already partially implemented | Requires code changes in write handlers | **RECOMMENDED** |\n| Lower TTL | Simple to implement | Doesn't solve problem, just reduces window; hurts performance | NOT RECOMMENDED |\n| Write-through cache | Guarantees consistency | Higher write latency, complex to implement for paginated queries | OVERKILL |\n| Event-driven invalidation | Decoupled, scalable | Adds infrastructure complexity, eventual consistency | FOR FUTURE |\n\n### Justification\n\n1. **Immediate Consistency**: Financial data requires accurate, real-time reporting. Serving stale balances or ledger entries is unacceptable in B2B reconciliation.\n\n2. **Infrastructure Already Exists**: The `PagedCache::evict()` method in module_46 and the pattern in module_67 show the architecture already supports invalidation\u2014it just needs to be wired up.\n\n3. **Targeted Invalidation**: Using key patterns (e.g., `tenant:{id}:ledger_entry:*`) allows efficient bulk invalidation without flushing the entire cache.\n\n4. **Distributed Support**: The pub/sub mechanism in module_46 (`INVALIDATION_CHANNEL`) enables fan-out to all service instances in a horizontally-scaled deployment.\n\n## Implementation Plan\n\n### Modules Requiring Modification\n\n1. **Write Handler Modules** (must ADD cache invalidation calls):\n   - `module_38.txt` (LedgerEntryPgRepository::insert)\n   - `module_71.txt` (CashFlowForecastService - add mutation handlers)\n   - Any other modules with POST/PUT/DELETE handlers for ledger entries\n\n2. **Caching Modules** (may need enhancement):\n   - `module_44.txt` - Add `invalidate_tenant_entries()` method\n   - `module_46.txt` - Already has `evict()`, may need to be exposed more broadly\n   - `module_33.txt` - Ensure `invalidate()` method is accessible\n\n### New Interactions Required\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510      \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510      \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  Write Handler  \u2502 \u2500\u2500\u2500\u25ba \u2502  Database (PG)   \u2502      \u2502  Cache (Redis)  \u2502\n\u2502  (module_38)    \u2502      \u2502                  \u2502      \u2502                 \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518      \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518      \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u25b2\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n         \u2502                                                   \u2502\n         \u2502  2. Add invalidation method:**\n```rust\nimpl<R> LedgerEntryQuerySvc<R> {\n    /// Invalidate all cached entries for a tenant\n    pub async fn invalidate_tenant(&self, tenant: Uuid) -> Result<(), ServiceError> {\n        let pattern = format!(\"ledger_entries:{}:*\", tenant);\n        let mut conn = self.redis.get().await?;\n        let keys: Vec<String> = redis::cmd(\"KEYS\")\n            .arg(&pattern)\n            .query_async(&mut conn)\n            .await?;\n        if !keys.is_empty() {\n            redis::cmd(\"UNLINK\")\n                .arg(&keys)\n                .query_async(&mut conn)\n                .await?;\n        }\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**module_71.txt - Read operations cache responses in Redis, but write operations (POST/PUT/DELETE) do not invalidate the corresponding cache entries, causing clients to receive outdated data until TTL expiration.\n\n- **Key components**:\n  - Caching: `module_44`, `module_46`, `module_33`\n  - Read handlers: `module_26`, `module_52`, `module_71`\n  - Write handlers: `module_38`, `module_67`\n\n- **Architectural pattern**: The system uses CQRS (Command Query Responsibility Segregation) with a cache-aside pattern. The cache layer exists and has invalidation infrastructure (`PagedCache::evict()`, `ResponseCache::invalidate()`), but write handlers are not wired to call these methods.\n\n- **Root cause**: Write handlers in modules like `module_38` and most mutations do NOT call cache invalidation after successful database writes. The exception is `module_67::create_entry()` which properly invalidates cache\u2014this pattern needs to be replicated across all write handlers.\n\n- **Recommendations**:\n  1. Modify all write handlers (`module_38`, `module_71`, etc.) to call `cache.invalidate()` after successful DB writes\n  2. Use key pattern matching (e.g., `tenant:{id}:*`) for efficient bulk invalidation\n  3. Leverage existing pub/sub infrastructure (`INVALIDATION_CHANNEL`) for distributed cache coherence\n  4. Do NOT simply lower TTL\u2014this is ineffective for financial data consistency and hurts cache hit rates\n",

# Solution: rust_api_microservice_expert_008_architectural_understanding_expert_01

## Executive Summary

The LedgerLink Nexus service suffers from a **cache invalidation problem** where read handlers populate a Redis response cache on cache misses, but write handlers (POST/PUT/DELETE operations) **do not invalidate** or update the corresponding cache entries. This causes clients to receive stale data until the cache entry's TTL expires naturally.

## Key Files Identified

### Core Caching Modules
- `/app/project/src/module_44.txt` - **Primary caching module**: High-volume Ledger Entry listing with Redis response-level caching. Contains `LedgerEntryQuerySvc` with `try_fetch_cache()` and `persist_cache()` methods, but only READ operations interact with cache.
- `/app/project/src/module_46.txt` - **Pagination-aware Redis cache**: Contains `PagedCache<T>` with an explicit `evict()` method that *should* be called by write handlers but isn't wired to them.
- `/app/project/src/module_33.txt` - **ResponseCache trait**: Defines cache abstraction with `invalidate()` method but write handlers don't use it.

### Read Handler Modules (Query Side)
- `/app/project/src/module_26.txt` - Ledger Entry Query Endpoint: Implements `get_ledger_entries()` handler that checks Redis cache before querying the database, stores results in cache on miss.
- `/app/project/src/module_52.txt` - High-frequency paginated read-model for ledger entries with `LedgerEntryService::get_paginated()` that uses cache.
- `/app/project/src/module_71.txt` - Cash-Flow Forecast query service with Redis-backed response caching.

### Write Handler Modules (Command Side)
- `/app/project/src/module_67.txt` - **Contains BOTH read and write operations**: Has `create_entry()` which properly invalidates cache (the exception),
... (truncated)
